# Alliance for the Chesapeake Bay — Native Plant Catalog

**Source:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/  
**Total plants:** 417  
**Scraped:** 2026-03-23

---

## Acer negundo

**Common Names:** box elder, ash leaf maple, Manitoba maple  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/acer-negundo/  

- **Family:** Aceraceae
- **Plant Type:** Small/Medium Tree (Understory)
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 30 - 60ft
- **Spread:** 30 - 60ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Clay, Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** April - May
- **Fall Color:** yellow, red
- **Fruit:** Winged; Brown
- **Habitat:** grows best in lowland sites along rivers, streams, ponds, and seasonally flooded areas; tolerates a variety of soil types
- **Notes:** brittle wood; thicket-forming; Sometimes planted as a fast-growing, short lived shade tree; squirrels and songbirds eat the seeds

---

## Acer rubrum

**Common Names:** red maple, scarlet maple, swamp maple, soft maple  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/acer-rubrum/  

- **Family:** Aceraceae
- **Plant Type:** Tall Tree (Canopy)
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 40 - 100ft
- **Spread:** 30 - 75ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Clay, Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** (inconspicuous)
- **Blooms:** March - April
- **Fall Color:** red, orange, yellow
- **Fruit:** Winged; Brown, Red, Yellow
- **Habitat:** swamps, uplands;  occasionally on dry rocky hillsides and sanddunes
- **Notes:** earliest spring bloomer; adaptable; This species is responsible for much of the fall coloration, running from purple to bright reds or yellows; the dry fruits are eaten by many birds and by squirrels; porcupines sometimes eat the inner bark and the twigs are a staple food of cottontail rabb

---

## Acer saccharinum

**Common Names:** silver maple, white maple, river maple, soft maple  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/acer-saccharinum/  

- **Family:** Aceraceae
- **Plant Type:** Tall Tree (Canopy)
- **Region:** Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 50 - 100ft
- **Spread:** 75 - 100ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Clay, Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** February - March
- **Fall Color:** yellow
- **Fruit:** Winged; Brown
- **Habitat:** wet, poorly drained, mucky or peaty soils of floodplains, streams, river bottoms, and along ponds and lakes
- **Notes:** ; Wood used for furniture making and woodworking; used as a shade tree, but limbs break easily with snow or ice storms; the dry fruits are eaten by many birds and by squirrels; porcupines sometimes eat the inner bark and the twigs are a staple food of cotto

- **Soil Moisture:** Dry, Moist
- **Flower Color:** White
- **Blooms:** July - October
- **Fruit:** Capsule;
- **Habitat:** rich woods, thickets, clearings, meadows
- **Notes:** tough plant; cultivars available; prefers basic soils; poisonous to livestock, causing trembling and loss of weight; very variable species

## Alnus serrulata

**Common Names:** smooth alder, hazel alder  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/alnus-serrulata/  

- **Family:** Betulaceae
- **Plant Type:** Tall Shrub
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 12 - 20ft
- **Spread:** 12 - 20ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Clay, Loamy
- **Soil Moisture:** Flooded, Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** Purple
- **Blooms:** March - April
- **Fall Color:** yellow, red
- **Fruit:** Cone/Cone-like; Brown
- **Habitat:** fresh tidal and nontidal marshes, shrub swamps, forested wetlands
- **Notes:** forms thickets along watercourses; nitrogen fixing; tolerates flooding to 3"; used by deer and beaver; the seeds are eaten by ruffed grouse, goldfinch, and a few other songbirds

---

## Amelanchier arborea

**Common Names:** downy serviceberry, shadbush  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/amelanchier-arborea/  

- **Family:** Rosaceae
- **Plant Type:** Small/Medium Tree (Understory)
- **Region:** Mountain
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 15 - 25ft
- **Spread:** - ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Partial Sun, Shade
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Dry, Moist
- **Flower Color:** White
- **Blooms:** March - May
- **Fall Color:** yellow, red
- **Fruit:** Fleshy; Purple, Red
- **Habitat:** woods, along river banks, swamps, and rocky slopes; more common at lower elevations
- **Notes:** used by 58 wildlife species; 35 bird species; important early summer food; berries edible to people; Has been cut for mine props, charcoal and sometimes used for handles; furnish browse for deer; the fruits are eaten by many species of songbirds and also by bear, and squirrels

---

- **Plant Type:** Vine
- **Region:** Mountain
- **States:** Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 20 - 36ft
- **Spread:** - ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist
- **Flower Color:** Purple, Yellow
- **Blooms:** May - June
- **Fall Color:** yellow green
- **Fruit:** Pod; Brown, Green
- **Habitat:** rich woods, and banks of streams
- **Notes:** occasionally escapes from cultivation; host for pipevine swallowtail butterfly; endangered in MD, grows best in deep loams

## Betula alleghaniensis

**Common Names:** yellow birch  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/betula-alleghaniensis/  

- **Family:** Betulaceae
- **Plant Type:** Tall Tree (Canopy)
- **Region:** Mountain
- **States:** Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 60 - 80ft
- **Spread:** 35 - 50ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** April - May
- **Fall Color:** golden yellow
- **Fruit:** Cone/Cone-like; Brown, Green
- **Habitat:** moist, rich uplands to low-lying swamps and borders of streams, elevated floodplain terrace and knobs
- **Notes:** fall color; attractive winter texture and color; prefers cool, moist conditions, common on calcareous soils; B. lutea syn for B. all. var. all. Wood used for furniture, cabinet work, mine props, charcoal and pulpwood; whitetail deer and cottontail rabbit utilize this tree for food; oil of wintergreen from bark and stem (Dirr)

- **Notes:** excellent fall color; prefers moist sites, tolerates dry; colonizes open or disturbed areas; Seedlings invade open fields and road banks, often forming nearly pure stands; wood used for cabinet work, plywood, charcoal, mine props and pulp wood; buds and seeds are eaten by ruffed and sharptail grouse; twigs browsed by whitetail deer and cottontail

- **Spread:** 35 - 50ft

- **Soil Texture:** Clay, Loamy
- **Soil Moisture:** Dry, Moist
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** June - June
- **Fall Color:** yellow or purple
- **Fruit:** Berry; Orange, Purple
- **Habitat:** open, disturbed areas and deciduous woodlands
- **Notes:** edible fruits; Wood used for shuttles, golf clubs, billiard cues, brushes; ripe, soft, and full colored persimmons are delicious; deer eat twigs, leaves and fruit of the persimmon; fruits important in the diet of foxes, opossum, raccoon

## Fagus grandifolia

- **Plant Type:** Tall Tree (Canopy)
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia

- **Spread:** 50 - 75ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** April - May
- **Fall Color:** yellow/tan; retains leaves till spring
- **Fruit:** Nut/Nut-like; Green, Orange
- **Habitat:** variety of soils, moist rich uplands and lowlands
- **Notes:** edible nuts; attractive bark; leaves may persist into winter; max ht 70? Used for furniture, pulpwood, charcoal and low grade lumber; excellent for fuel; deer browse the twigs and foliage to some extent; the nuts are eaten by ruffed grouse, wild turkey, squirrel, black bear and raccoon

- **Fruit:** Cone/Cone-like; Blue, Green

- **Notes:** berries consumed by over 50 species of birds; berries have culinary use; Heartwood is light, strong, durable, and widely used for cedar chests, cabinets, lead pencils, fuel, and fence posts; birds pass the seeds through their digestive tracts undamaged, particularly along fencelines

- **Plant Type:** Tall Tree (Canopy)
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 70 - 100ft
- **Spread:** 35 - 50ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Full Sun, Partial Sun
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Moist
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** June - June
- **Fall Color:** yellow
- **Fruit:** Winged; Brown
- **Habitat:** bottomlands in wet to mesic woods, mountain coves, and lower slopes
- **Notes:** fast growth; Used for veneer, furniture, house siding and construction; a useful fast-growing timber tree; one of the tallest eastern trees; is second to only to Sycamore in trunk diameter; the seeds are eaten by squirrels and a few songbirds, especially the cardinal;

- **Soil Moisture:** Moist, Wet
- **Flower Color:** Pink, White
- **Blooms:** May - August
- **Fall Color:** yellow, orange, to purple
- **Fruit:** Capsule; Brown
- **Habitat:** low wet floodplain woods and depressions, sluggish streambanks, swamp borders, hillside bogs, ditch banks, clearings
- **Notes:** attractive spreading, loose-branched habit; demands acid soil; susceptible to disease and insects

---

## Rhus aromatica

**Common Names:** fragrant sumac  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/rhus-aromatica/  

- **Family:** Anacardiaceae
- **Plant Type:** Medium Shrub
- **Region:** Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** District of Columbia, Maryland, New York, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 6 - 6ft
- **Spread:** 12 - 12ft

- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Dry
- **Flower Color:** Green, Yellow
- **Blooms:** March - May
- **Fall Color:** red
- **Fruit:** Berry; Red
- **Habitat:** limestone cliffs, dry open upland woods, open rocky bluffs, oak barrens and openings, foredunes, barren rock
- **Notes:** fuzzy edible berry clusters; aromatic leaves; shorter cultivars available; male and female separate plants; all of our upland gamebirds and many species of songbirds eat the seeds and fruits; deer browse the foliage and cottontail rabbits feed on the twigs and bark; flowers much used by bees

- **Notes:** sweet berries; Berries sweet, of excellent flavor, and much used for pies, muffins; furnish browse for deer; the fruits are eaten by ruffed grouse, wild turkey, black bear, squirrels, raccoon, foxes, other mammals and many species of songbirds

## Cercis canadensis

**Common Names:** eastern redbud  
**URL:** https://www.allianceforthebay.org/plants/cercis-canadensis/  

- **Family:** Fabaceae
- **Plant Type:** Small/Medium Tree (Understory)
- **Region:** Coastal Plain, Mountain, Piedmont
- **States:** Delaware, District of Columbia, Maryland, Pennsylvania, Virginia, West Virginia
- **Height:** 20 - 35ft
- **Spread:** 20 - 35ft
- **Sun Exposure:** Partial Sun, Shade
- **Soil Texture:** Loamy, Sandy
- **Soil Moisture:** Dry, Moist
- **Flower Color:** Pink
- **Blooms:** April - May
- **Fall Color:** golden yellow
- **Fruit:** Pod; Black
- **Habitat:** rich, moist sites; prefers river bottoms and stream banks
- **Notes:** purple flowers in spring, about same time as flowering dogwood; fixes nitrogen; Useful as an ornamental; showy reddish springtime flowers; seeds or pods eaten by pheasants and deer
